---
title: "11.04 OpenGL\3D not working, renderer is &quot;Software Rasterizer&quot;"
date: 2011-05-31
forum: Hardware
---

### Post by Agent24 on 2011-05-31
After having a problem with performance as detailed in [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=10887350](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=10887350) I realised it's a problem with my OpenGL\3D acceleration.

My OpenGL Renderer is "Software Rasterizer" but I don't know how to fix it.

As I said in the other post, it worked fine on the first install but not on a reinstall, so I know it CAN work, it just isn't working now.

I am using a Radeon 9600 XT with of course the 'radeon' driver.

---

### Post by Yellow Pasque on 2011-05-31
Post your /var/log/Xorg.0.log

---

### Post by Agent24 on 2011-06-01
OK this is very strange...

This morning when I started up, my resolution had been reset to 800x600, but not only that I noticed an improved performance in general in the GUI.

When changing the resolution back to the usual I also noticed that it was detecting a 2nd monitor (actually my television) even though I only have the S-video cable connected to the video card and not the TV on the other end.

(I keep the cable plugged in because it's easier than trying to plug it back in every time I want to use TV-out - which by the way I only use in Windows, because I have never managed to get it to work in Linux)

Anyway, strangely enough today the Gallium driver is working, because now I get:
[B]```
OpenGL vendor string: X.Org R300 Project
OpenGL renderer string: Gallium 0.4 on ATI RV350

```[/B]
Instead of previously:
[B]```
OpenGL vendor string: Mesa Project
OpenGL renderer string: Software Rasterizer

```[/B]

### Post by Agent24 on 2011-06-05
Well I've played around with cables attached, not attached, and the only thing that seems consistent is that 3D Acceleration and TV Detection go hand-in-hand.

If the TV is detected (doesn't matter if it's plugged in or not) then 3D\Gallium is enabled and works.
If it doesn't detect the TV then 3D also falls back to software mode.

Also it seems TV detection (or not) only works properly on a cold boot, not a restart etc.


On the up-side, the TV-out actually works in this version of Ubuntu (previous versions detected the TV but wouldn't display anything on it)

---
